  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4ef2b4c7-f745-4480-ac52-9941ca0ac6da'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer15711739787989013773">A captivating true story of loyalty, friendship, and high adventure that spans several decades and three continents, <em>Modoc</em> is one of the most remarkable true stories ever told, perfect for fans of <em>The Zookeeper's Wife </em>or <em>Water for Elephants</em>.<br/><br/>Raised together in a small German circus town, a boy and an elephant formed a bond that would last their entire lives, and would be te</span>
  <span id="freeText15711739787989013773" style="display:none">A captivating true story of loyalty, friendship, and high adventure that spans several decades and three continents, <em>Modoc</em> is one of the most remarkable true stories ever told, perfect for fans of <em>The Zookeeper's Wife </em>or <em>Water for Elephants</em>.<br /><br />Raised together in a small German circus town, a boy and an elephant formed a bond that would last their entire lives, and would be tested time and again: through a near-fatal shipwreck in the Indian Ocean, an apprenticeship with the legendary Mahout elephant trainers in the Indian teak forests, and their eventual rise to circus stardom in 1940s New York City.  As the <em>African Sun-Times </em>put it, <em>Modoc </em>is "heartwarming...probably the greatest love story ever told."<br /><br />"Once I started this incomparable story, I couldn't put it down, and I cannot get it out of my mind--nor will I ever. The message of what can be accomplished by training through affection and joy will thrill all animal lovers." -- Betty White</span>
  <a data-text-id="15711739787989013773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_420042453" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420042453" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5211606-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505571524p2/5211606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420042453?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/5211606-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=nobody-talks-like-this">nobody-talks-like-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=don-t-believe-the-hype">don-t-believe-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420042453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10847749112525945644">The ONLY reason I read past page 3 was that this was a book club pick. If I were to teach a class in creative writing right now, I would use this book as an example of what NOT to do in your writing. First, is it fiction or non-fiction? Seems that the "author" is claiming non-fiction, but this story is terribly contrived and rings as untrue in almost every chapter. The dialogue is positively laughable. It was hilarious that all of the characters from all of the different countries all spoke the </span>
  <span id="freeText10847749112525945644" style="display:none">The ONLY reason I read past page 3 was that this was a book club pick. If I were to teach a class in creative writing right now, I would use this book as an example of what NOT to do in your writing. First, is it fiction or non-fiction? Seems that the "author" is claiming non-fiction, but this story is terribly contrived and rings as untrue in almost every chapter. The dialogue is positively laughable. It was hilarious that all of the characters from all of the different countries all spoke the same way. Somehow, the uneducated "Bram" spoke flawless English even though he had never left his little village in Germany and had no schooling or parents who spoke English. Also, there was no character development or sense of space or time. It could have taken place in any time and in any country (and I don't mean that in a good way). When I saw this book had an average review of 4.19, I took the time to read through several of them and see what I had missed. Most of the high reviews read, "I love elephants." And, "I love animals." Really? That is not a book review. If you love elephants, go to Africa. If you love books about animals, go read Old Yeller. This was a horrible waste of my time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10847749112525945644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer141823819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6274874967493945688">I gave this book one star because Mr. Helfer has passed it off as a true story, when clearly, it is not. Apparently, there was indeed an elephant named Modoc—there were six documented with that name, in fact. Yet, any reader with a critical eye can see that this is a tale of pure fantasy, with only the most distant connection to truth. <br/><br/>The events of the story are certainly exciting and provide a good plot line, full of adventure and drama, especially for an animal lover such as myself, but there</span>
  <span id="freeText6274874967493945688" style="display:none">I gave this book one star because Mr. Helfer has passed it off as a true story, when clearly, it is not. Apparently, there was indeed an elephant named Modoc—there were six documented with that name, in fact. Yet, any reader with a critical eye can see that this is a tale of pure fantasy, with only the most distant connection to truth. <br /><br />The events of the story are certainly exciting and provide a good plot line, full of adventure and drama, especially for an animal lover such as myself, but there isn't an ounce of realism to it. The events unfold with one amazing happening after another, complete with a shipwreck and subsequent rescue, a secret voyage of a boy and his elephant through the Indian jungle, the killing of several bandit men by the elephant in fierce protection of the boy, a Burmese village being overtaken by renegade soldiers, the execution of a man by elephant stomping, a battle scene during which several soldiers and the boy's young bride are killed, an elephant falling off a cliff, two weddings, a fatal circus fire (this event did happen, at least), the blinding of the elephant by a drunkard with a bull hook, the poisoning of all the elephants in the circus, followed by the last minute discovery of an antidote, and finally, the reunion of the boy and elephant after ten years apart at none other than the author's ranch in CA, where through miracle of miracles, Modoc the elephant has found refuge. (Oh, Please!) <br /><br />Meanwhile, the two love stories within this tale are terribly embarrassing and schmaltzy. The dialogue has an awkward, artificial quality, and lacks realism. And not surprisingly, the characters fall into two camps: the good guys and the bad guys. The good guys are really good and the bad guys are really bad! There is no subtlety, no nuance, and no complexity or personality. <br /><br />Now, if this book were written as a fable or a myth, especially for young readers, it would make much more sense. As a fable, it is a wonderful tale, full of life lessons, exotic places, rites of passage, tragedy, adventure, the struggle of good versus evil, and a bit of spirituality to boot. The dialogue is more appropriate as part of a mythical story, with universal lessons. And with such high drama, it is a page turner of a tale. Shame on Mr. Helfer for misrepresenting it as fact. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6274874967493945688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

If you like books about amazing animals and what they do - this is for you.   <span id="freeText13144443389774525969" style="display:none">An utterly amazing true story about an elephant, Mosie, and her trainer, Bram! If you like books about amazing animals and what they do - this is for you. Shipwrecks, fires, poisoning, terrorist revolutionary uprisings, teak forests, upspritualism and an anazing love story between one man and his elephant! This book is very plot driven. The bits on spiritualism didn't quite get me thinking.... I would say yup, I agree, and then that was the end. Nothing to ponder over. For example - one love never diminishes another love. <br /><br />I don't quite know if I pick light books over Xmas b/c I know my emotions will be fully occupied with family matters - the result being that I never find fabulous books over Christmas. Don't get me wrong, this is definitely worth the time I spent reading it, and I do recommend it, but it is no thought provoking book! The writing is clear, but that is it! I wouldn't say it sparkled. Does every book sparkle? One thing annoyed me - there was no map and dates were sparse. For example where exactly were those teak forests and where was the maharaja's Elephantarium or what city was it near? I like to know this stuff <br /><br />Before reading the book: I need to read something over Xmas that will grab me, usually my brain tends to stray! Check out the cover - can you see the little boy's hand around that elephant, the turn of the elephant's head, and the straightness of the little boy's back? A picture can say a thousand words.<br /><br />PLEASE TAKE THE TIME TO READ THE FIRST CHAPTER OF THIS BOOK AVAILABLE BOTHAT AMAZON AND B&amp;N!</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=read-on-recommendation">read-on-recommendation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42780923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11642002868880329969"> Before there was Dumbo, before but not quite before there was Toomai of the Elephants, there was Modoc and there was Bram, the boy who loved her. Boy and elephant, born on the same day, in the same hour, two souls intertwined throughout a lifetime.<br/><br/>This true story starts out in Germany, but soon travels the world. More adventures than you can count, a fearsome storm and shipwreck that rival (or maybe inspired) Life of Pi, life with princes in India, not to mention the legendary Mahout elephant t</span>
  <span id="freeText11642002868880329969" style="display:none"> Before there was Dumbo, before but not quite before there was Toomai of the Elephants, there was Modoc and there was Bram, the boy who loved her. Boy and elephant, born on the same day, in the same hour, two souls intertwined throughout a lifetime.<br /><br />This true story starts out in Germany, but soon travels the world. More adventures than you can count, a fearsome storm and shipwreck that rival (or maybe inspired) Life of Pi, life with princes in India, not to mention the legendary Mahout elephant trainers in the teak forests, a white elephant spiritual guide, circus time, love, loyalty...it's got it all! Bram and Modoc certainly seem to be soul mates of a sort, though Bram was lucky enough to find women who understood his love for an elephant as well as good and true friends in his lifetime. I loved the way Bram developed his on personal philosophy/spirituality that combined what he knew and what he learned from the elephant and mahouts.<br /><br />Ralph Helfer's style is a little stilted, but serves him well enough. He is best known as the Hollywood animal trainer who was one of the first to use affection and kindness to train the wild animals we see in movies and on TC. (Clarence the Cross_Eyed Lion is one of his most famous friends.)<br /><br />This book was given to me by TheSIL and I thoroughly enjoyed it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11642002868880329969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41202879" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41202879" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87252-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180751323p2/87252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41202879?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/87252-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87252-leah?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87252-leah?shelf=book-discussion">book-discussion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87252-leah?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41202879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16937566053822925232">Seriously? This book was total twaddle. I wasn't touched, I didn't cry, and I didn't emotionally react to any of the one-dimensional characters. Let's get this straight -- after floating in water during a hurricane for many days, the boy refuses to get on a boat to go to safety because the elephant can't come. After a few more days of floating, he decides to give up, and just as he's dipping under the water, ready to take in a breath of water, he hears a boat motor. It's a Christmas miracle! Des</span>
  <span id="freeText16937566053822925232" style="display:none">Seriously? This book was total twaddle. I wasn't touched, I didn't cry, and I didn't emotionally react to any of the one-dimensional characters. Let's get this straight -- after floating in water during a hurricane for many days, the boy refuses to get on a boat to go to safety because the elephant can't come. After a few more days of floating, he decides to give up, and just as he's dipping under the water, ready to take in a breath of water, he hears a boat motor. It's a Christmas miracle! Despite what should have been high winds and waves, he hears a motor. Under water. Am I just cynical?<br /><br />Also, one moment Bram is a boy, the next he's skinny dipping with a girl named Girtie. There's actually a surprising number of scenes where he's naked. Why? Doesn't seem to fit in the story at all.<br /><br />Now how about this writing?<br /><br />Actual sentences: "One afternoon as Bram dozed on his mat atop Modoc's back she stopped... abruptly!"<br /><br />"With great shoving and lifting of tonnage... slowly... Modoc stood!"<br /><br />"This was indeed the hospital... a hospital for elephants."<br /><br />The use of the word "din" multiple times reminded me of the sentences kids have to write after learning a new word. Give it a rest, man. <br /><br />And there's no way that most of this was fact. I should have never read the acknowledgments before I started the book. When mind reading and "energy" and "metaphysical" were mentioned, directly before the author's note that basically said that he may or may not be getting most things right, I was thinking, "Ruh roh."<br /><br />I noticed that several other reviewers noticed that Modoc's tusks were mysteriously absent in the pictures. Others noticed that the amount of time Helfer had with her didn't match up. One reviewer on Amazon mentioned that she tried looking into the information and couldn't find anything other than mentions of this book. No sources, no exact times or dates, and mostly inner dialogue (or dialogue with an elephant). But who knows, maybe all I've learned about finding and citing information is claptrap. Whoops, I meant to say, "Maybe all I've learned was... claptrap!"<br /><br />Even if this book was filed under fiction instead, nothing could save it from being poorly written melodramatic drivel. That being said, the children's book was quite lovely. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16937566053822925232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144213523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144213523" />
    <a title="Paul Pessolano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4877713-paul-pessolano"><img alt="Paul Pessolano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304961177p2/4877713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144213523?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Pessolano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Pessolano" href="/user/show/4877713-paul-pessolano">Paul Pessolano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144213523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14458232477457506604">This book was first published in 1997. I have been looking at it over the last several years promising myself that I would read it. I was fascinated by the cover and the reviews. The cover alone should have you reading the book. My only regret is that I did not read it the first time I saw it.<br/><br/>"Modoc" is probably the most unusual pet book I have ever read. It is hard to believe that this is a "true story".<br/><br/>Bram Gunterstein was the son of a circus animal trainer. He was born on his father's farm an</span>
  <span id="freeText14458232477457506604" style="display:none">This book was first published in 1997. I have been looking at it over the last several years promising myself that I would read it. I was fascinated by the cover and the reviews. The cover alone should have you reading the book. My only regret is that I did not read it the first time I saw it.<br /><br />"Modoc" is probably the most unusual pet book I have ever read. It is hard to believe that this is a "true story".<br /><br />Bram Gunterstein was the son of a circus animal trainer. He was born on his father's farm and, at the same time, an elephant to be named "Modoc" was born in the farm's barn.<br /><br />Bram and Modoc grew up together and formed a relationship that would be like no other. Bram's father believed that animals were to be trained with kindness and understanding, instead of with a whip. It is this context that Modoc took commands from Bram. Sometimes they seemed to be able to read each other's thoughts.<br /><br />The closing of the circus and Bram's fathers death caused Modoc to be sold to a circus operating in the United States. Bram was not part of the deal and his love for Modoc forced him to stow away on the ship transporting Modoc to the States. The ship runs into a typhoon and is sunk. Modoc and Bram survive and help in the rescue of other passengers. Modoc, at the point of drowning, is saved and both he and Bram are courted as heroes in India.<br /><br />The circus owner, in trying to find Modoc, causes Bram and Modoc to travel to the teak forests of India to work. They are captured by militants and almost die in traversing the mountains in India and engaging in a gunfight between the militants and the Indian Government. Both Modoc and Bram are injured, Modoc seriously, but they both pull through and find themselves attached to the circus in the United States.<br /><br />The book is filled with unbelievable love, caring, and devotion between Bram and Modoc. I cannot imagine or think of a human/animal relationship that even comes close to what they had. A magnificent read for those who just want to read a good book, or one who loves books about animals, or one who likes a book where relationships really matter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14458232477457506604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12773912?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Opal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Opal" href="/user/show/796131-opal">Opal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12773912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2918182427007050072">I think this is a wonderful story, but it is not written well at all. This books is written by an animal trainer, and on the one hand, I commend him for doing such a great job, but on the other hand, writing is clearly not his calling.<br/><br/>That being said, he is writing a so-called "true story" but most of the book is written from the point of view of someone else, so you lose some of the first hand experience. Therefore, the title character seems to lack feeling and emotion. The author does state at</span>
  <span id="freeText2918182427007050072" style="display:none">I think this is a wonderful story, but it is not written well at all. This books is written by an animal trainer, and on the one hand, I commend him for doing such a great job, but on the other hand, writing is clearly not his calling.<br /><br />That being said, he is writing a so-called "true story" but most of the book is written from the point of view of someone else, so you lose some of the first hand experience. Therefore, the title character seems to lack feeling and emotion. The author does state at the beginning that he may have added in some of his own parts, obviously conversations, which led me to question a lot of what happened in this book. I think it is an incredible story, and Bram and Modoc went on incredible adventures, but I have to wonder how "true" each parts are. <br /><br />If you move past what is "true" this is really an amazing story of the bond between man and animal, and how smart elephants truly are. Not knowing a lot about elephants, there are very descriptive passages about how elephants are, their abilities, and it is so interesting. <br /><br />I honestly could get past some of the poor writing though and I couldn't put this book down. Of course, it has a happy ending as well, and that always helps.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288815401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16445089273562357593">Highly disappointing and frustrating! Fiction, posing as a non-fiction biography. And not even well-written fiction. What a con!!! I'm stunned that so many people rated this so highly, and without questioning any or all of its validity. <br/><br/>Very little, if anything is "True" in Helfer's book. The longer I read the more red-flags went up left and right questioning the legitimacy of its contents. So many people/places/things were nowhere to be found upon researching. But when Helfer described Modoc as</span>
  <span id="freeText16445089273562357593" style="display:none">Highly disappointing and frustrating! Fiction, posing as a non-fiction biography. And not even well-written fiction. What a con!!! I'm stunned that so many people rated this so highly, and without questioning any or all of its validity. <br /><br />Very little, if anything is "True" in Helfer's book. The longer I read the more red-flags went up left and right questioning the legitimacy of its contents. So many people/places/things were nowhere to be found upon researching. But when Helfer described Modoc as having tusks, lifting teakwood, that was it for me. Female Asian elephants do not have tusks. Furthermore, the photos in this book of supposedly Modoc in her latter years, depict a rather small Asian elephant sans scarring; obviously not the grandiose pachyderm described as having been subjected to much abuse that would have left quite recognizable scars. And the icing on the cake: Researching Ralph Helfer's verifiable history, produces numerous accounts of lawsuits and injunctions brought against him, which include, among other financial/ethical things, animal neglect/abuse/endangerment. <br /><br />Sad....Sad....Sad.... The things people will do to make a buck and the things people believe without question, is mind blowing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16445089273562357593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130260094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6805087475620471496">I wanted to like this book, especially as it was recommended to me, and I do hate when I don't like something someone else really liked. But I had a lot of trouble with this. First, I am not really sure it's a true story. In fact, I am pretty convinced it's NOT. I can't find any corroborating information to prove to me it was--about ANY of the events in the story. There was not a single date mentioned. Not Bram's birthday or death, or many other dates of great significance. <br/><br/>Now, if it HAD been a</span>
  <span id="freeText6805087475620471496" style="display:none">I wanted to like this book, especially as it was recommended to me, and I do hate when I don't like something someone else really liked. But I had a lot of trouble with this. First, I am not really sure it's a true story. In fact, I am pretty convinced it's NOT. I can't find any corroborating information to prove to me it was--about ANY of the events in the story. There was not a single date mentioned. Not Bram's birthday or death, or many other dates of great significance. <br /><br />Now, if it HAD been a true story, I would have been OK with the writing. After all, it's an animal trainer, not a writer who wrote it. I am OK with a little roughness. But as I think it's fiction . . . well then the writing should be better. <br /><br />It could have been an awe-inspiring true story. Or it could have been a riveting adventure tale and love story, perhaps if written in the style of Water for Elephants. But it can't choose what it wants to be, so it falls flat for me.<br /> <br />I will say my favorite part was Bram and Modoc's travels through India, which reminded me of Rudyard Kipling's Kim. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6805087475620471496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217316119" />
    <a title="Louise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2143983-louise"><img alt="Louise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295627785p2/2143983.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217316119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7640798963390875790">Story Description:<br/><br/>Modoc is the joint biography of a man and an elephant born in a small German circus town on the same day in 1896. Bram was the son of an elephant trainer, Modoc the daughter of his prize performer. The boy and animal grew up devoted to each other. When the Wunderzircus was sold to an American, with no provision to take along the human staff, Bram stowed away on the ship to prevent being separated from his beloved Modoc. A shipwreck off the Indian coast and a sojourn with a maha</span>
  <span id="freeText7640798963390875790" style="display:none">Story Description:<br /><br />Modoc is the joint biography of a man and an elephant born in a small German circus town on the same day in 1896. Bram was the son of an elephant trainer, Modoc the daughter of his prize performer. The boy and animal grew up devoted to each other. When the Wunderzircus was sold to an American, with no provision to take along the human staff, Bram stowed away on the ship to prevent being separated from his beloved Modoc. A shipwreck off the Indian coast and a sojourn with a maharajah were only the beginning of the pair's incredible adventures. They battled bandits, armed revolutionaries, cruel animal trainers, and greedy circus owners in their quest to stay together. They triumphed against the odds and thrilled American circus audiences with Modoc's dazzling solo performances, only to be torn apart with brutal suddenness, seemingly never to meet again. Hollywood animal trainer Ralph Helfer rescued Modoc from ill-treatment and learned her astonishing story when Bram rediscovered her at Helfer's company. His emotional retelling of this true-life adventure epic will make pulses race and bring tears to readers' eyes. <br /><br />My Review:<br /><br />“Modoc is a love story, a gut-wrenching afternoon kind of love story that should not be attempted without a full box if tissues within easy reach.” –Detroit Free Free<br /><br />“…sweeping across the timber land into the gray, misty valleys of the Black Forest…baby sounds! Below the fog layer, the insistent waits a baby could be heard, their temerity as if from Mother Earth herself.<br /><br />And then another voice arose. Deeper, brassy, trumpety, but still a…baby sound.”<br /><br />Thus begins the true story of Modoc. Bram, borne to Josef and Katrina Gutterstein, and named after Josef’s father, was a beautiful baby boy with blonde hair. Bram’s blonde hair and features came from the strong Nordic ide of Katrina’s family, and the sweet and gentle warmth radiated so strongly from Josef’s heritage. They lived in Hangendorf Valley, Germany and Josef just knew that Bram would be would become: “a fine elephant trainer.<br /><br />Josef himself is an elelphant trainer working for a small circus in the nearby<br /> town of Hassengross. Emma, had just given birth to her elephant up, “Modoc” and Josef was determined to make Emma’s baby the best trained elephant the world has even seen. If anyone could do it, he could as his whole family was circus and the last three generations were all elephant trainers when Josef’s own son Bram, was old enough, he would be turned over to him from training and he’d follow in his father’s footsteps.<br /><br />I immediately fell in love in love with “Modoc’ and “Bram”. This large mammal and young boy had a bond like no other I’ve ever seen. The closeness, the love, the depth of the relationship was beyond anything I had ever encountered. A most mesmerizing story not to be missed!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7640798963390875790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416948-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520585274?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/1416948-susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520585274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14552618228174628429">What a bizarre book! Most of the book seems like stories a grandfather would make up for his grandchildren about the former life of their pet dog they adopted at the pound. Even the youngest of the grandchildren would realize that these crazy adventures did not really happen.<br/><br/>Then there are a few scenes in the book that make you wonder if you had accidentally picked up a completely different, and much darker, book. There is a prolonged and graphic attempted rape part that makes one think we shoul</span>
  <span id="freeText14552618228174628429" style="display:none">What a bizarre book! Most of the book seems like stories a grandfather would make up for his grandchildren about the former life of their pet dog they adopted at the pound. Even the youngest of the grandchildren would realize that these crazy adventures did not really happen.<br /><br />Then there are a few scenes in the book that make you wonder if you had accidentally picked up a completely different, and much darker, book. There is a prolonged and graphic attempted rape part that makes one think we shouldn't leave grandad alone with the kids anymore. Why on Earth was that in this book?!<br /><br />There is absolutely no character development. Everyone is either good or bad. All of the good people are pretty much interchangeable in personality. There are a bunch of lines that are spoken as though profound, but are really nonsensical. The story is very choppy. Every so often, "many years" pass and there is no way to know what year it is or how old the characters are.<br /><br />Very early in the book, it will strike you that this is not really a true story at all and you will be distracted while reading it wondering why they have "True Story" in the title. You will need to work past your feelings of confusion and annoyance in order to finish the book. It is difficult, but possible. I did it, but the book did not get any better or any more realistic, so you may want to just give in to your feelings and stop reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14552618228174628429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_342055086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/342055086" />
    <a title="Kim Crane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3086933-kim-crane"><img alt="Kim Crane" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342055086?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim Crane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim Crane" href="/user/show/3086933-kim-crane">Kim Crane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342055086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2927532945324820433">I was exhilarated after reading this book. I wanted so badly to believe that this special elephant and this special boy and all of the incredible things that happened to them were true. I found the narrator off-putting through most of the book, but I forgave him because he brought me this beautiful (true!) story. I would have forgiven the extreme poetic license, laughable dialogue, and general editorial negligence if this book delivered what set the reader up for from the subtitle: The True Stor</span>
  <span id="freeText2927532945324820433" style="display:none">I was exhilarated after reading this book. I wanted so badly to believe that this special elephant and this special boy and all of the incredible things that happened to them were true. I found the narrator off-putting through most of the book, but I forgave him because he brought me this beautiful (true!) story. I would have forgiven the extreme poetic license, laughable dialogue, and general editorial negligence if this book delivered what set the reader up for from the subtitle: The True Story of the Greatest Elephant that Ever Lived. Unfortunately, while I managed to suspend my disbelief throughout the entire book, I made the mistake of trying to find out more about these remarkable protagonists after I finished. Some basic googling revealed the not entirely unexpected results that this story was probably way more fiction than fact. I couldn't find evidence to prove that the elephant Modoc, the human protagonist Bram, or any of the major plot points (some of which, like a shipwreck, would certainly have been documented) were real. Initially delightful, this book was ultimately disappointing. I can't recommend it as nonfiction, and I'm not sure I'd recommend it as fiction either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2927532945324820433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_30762527" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Clair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1443527-clair"><img alt="Clair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340920252p2/1443527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30762527?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clair" href="/user/show/1443527-clair">Clair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30762527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8253224482833121960">This story highlights a special relationship between an elephant and a boy who were born on the same day in Germany. Beginning as part of a circus family, the two spend the majority of their lives together surviving many obstacles and near-death experiences. The love Modoc and Bram have for each other and the way they are able to communicate is very inspiring. This part of the story I loved.<br/><br/>I thought some parts would have best been left out- some brief but graphic descriptions are used to relate</span>
  <span id="freeText8253224482833121960" style="display:none">This story highlights a special relationship between an elephant and a boy who were born on the same day in Germany. Beginning as part of a circus family, the two spend the majority of their lives together surviving many obstacles and near-death experiences. The love Modoc and Bram have for each other and the way they are able to communicate is very inspiring. This part of the story I loved.<br /><br />I thought some parts would have best been left out- some brief but graphic descriptions are used to relate violence that occurs when an elephant defends herself. And surely I could have been spared the details of elephant breeding. Too bad there wasn't an edited version of the book. <br /><br />I'm not sure how "true" to life it all is, though I'm sure the storyline and plot are based on real events. Helfer, the author of the story is someone who meets Modoc and Bram near the end of their lives. I imagine the author is mostly going off of stories he's been told. In an author's note, Helfer explains that he based his writing on what he knew was true, on research that may or not be true, and on hearsay. Then, of course, there is poetic license. So, while some parts are very beautiful and touching, I kept wondering which parts are based on reality and which are embellishments.<br /><br />Either way, Modoc and Bram are to be admired for their courage, love, and determination.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8253224482833121960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13701265266208932332" style="display:none">I felt like the writing of this story was faux-poetic in that the author was trying to be deep and moving, but was unsuccesful. I could get past the writing for the story, but I was bothered by the lack of any sense of time and by the ease by which this young man made his way from continent to continent- not that the traveling itself was easy, but he had no trouble fitting in to new environments where I would expect his age and linguistic knowledge to be a barrier. <div id="review_28884713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28884713" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/159993-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209224964p2/159993.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28884713?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/159993-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28884713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6495243078300651200">True story, my Aunt Ethel. While Modoc and Bram may have existed, this account of their lives is obviously wishful, and has little basis in reality. Helfer has apparently trained elephants for films, but he doesn't seem to know much about how they act in the wild. His account of breeding Asian elephants is full of factual errors, and he speaks of Modoc's tusks when, according to the photos included in the text, she never <i>had</i> tusks (as most female Asian elephants do not). What a waste of time.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3163575594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3163575594" />
    <a title="Pietavandyke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29447492-pietavandyke"><img alt="Pietavandyke" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3163575594?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pietavandyke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pietavandyke" href="/user/show/29447492-pietavandyke">Pietavandyke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3163575594&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3163575594" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15327922503088903852">On the cover it says "The True Story of the Greatest Elephant That Ever Lived" which threw me off, because I had always understood that Jumbo was the greatest circus elephant ever, but its not about him. And almost none of it is true. As I was reading of the adventures and misadventures of Bram and Modoc, I got more and more sceptical - if they were going by boat from Germany to the US, why would they go via India? How does a boy raised in rural Germany know how to speak English? How is he findi</span>
  <span id="freeText15327922503088903852" style="display:none">On the cover it says "The True Story of the Greatest Elephant That Ever Lived" which threw me off, because I had always understood that Jumbo was the greatest circus elephant ever, but its not about him. And almost none of it is true. As I was reading of the adventures and misadventures of Bram and Modoc, I got more and more sceptical - if they were going by boat from Germany to the US, why would they go via India? How does a boy raised in rural Germany know how to speak English? How is he finding so many people in disparate rural areas of India who can all speak English? How did they happen to survive the shipwreck and land a short walk from the largest elephant sanctuary/hospital in the whole country. By the end of the book I thought that maybe there was an elephant named Modoc with a German handler named Bram who ended up in a circus in the USA. So I held off until I was finished to do an internet search and found out that the author made it all up! The only thing thats true is that the author ran an animal rental agency for the film industry and he rescued a badly neglected elephant named Modoc who might have been one of three circus elephants named Modoc. And John North was a real circus entrepreneur who was related to the Ringling Brothers. Its too bad that it was portrayed as true, because its quite an entertaining read as it is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15327922503088903852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347420059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer152398442142370742"><i>Modoc: The True Story of the Greatest Elephant That Ever Lived</i> is one of the greatest stories that has ever been told. It took me a long time to read this book--not because I wasn't into it, but because I kept wanting to postpone the inevitable sob fest that was even referenced in a blurb on the book's cover. I felt such a myriad of emotions throughout the course of <i>Modoc</i>: childlike wonder, nostalgia, heart ache, pure joy, and nearly constant bursts of love.<br/><br/>From the Black Forest of Germany, to t</span>
  <span id="freeText152398442142370742" style="display:none"><i>Modoc: The True Story of the Greatest Elephant That Ever Lived</i> is one of the greatest stories that has ever been told. It took me a long time to read this book--not because I wasn't into it, but because I kept wanting to postpone the inevitable sob fest that was even referenced in a blurb on the book's cover. I felt such a myriad of emotions throughout the course of <i>Modoc</i>: childlike wonder, nostalgia, heart ache, pure joy, and nearly constant bursts of love.<br /><br />From the Black Forest of Germany, to the rain forests of India, and finally to the hustle and bustle of 1940's New York City, <i>Modoc</i> took me on an adventure I'll never forget and showcased a special bond between man and animal that spanned from birth to death and undoubtedly endures in the afterlife. I can't describe how truly special this book is. I finished it several days ago and just thinking about it in order to write this review has me all tear soaked and snotty again. These tears are the bittersweet kind, I promise. <br /><br />My heart is so full of <i>Modoc</i>, it could just bust. There aren't enough stars in the world for a book like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="152398442142370742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/vl/1YbGPwkwEVajOVVbDUapDoPpwvcHRMuDAkNhX9BNHEAOlXr4L9MJZjLzJgXByPv8c0xzqdWCOsEI9QCCFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

In a &quot;cull,&quot; her family was slaughtered. Only the newborn female\'s life was spared. Terrified and bewildered the young elephant was transported to America to be sold.\n\nBob Norris is a cowboy with an enormous empathy for animals. Handsome as a movie star, he was the Marlboro Man, with his face appearing on billboards around the world. But something was missing. When the hurt, vulnerable little elephant, Amy, came into his life, an incredible bond between the most unlikely of friends was forged.\n\nBob adopted Amy and through close observation, gentle training, humor, and endless perseverance, this accomplished horseman gradually coaxed Amy into overcoming her mistrust of humans, and her fear of the world. Amy became a beloved member of the Norris family, and partner to the ranch hands, but Bob knew from the start that the ultimate goal was for Amy to regain her confidence and her independence - even, if it were possible, to go back to the savannahs of Africa.\n\nAmy may have left the cowboy\'s life, but she never left his heart. The Cowboy and His Elephant is a story of mutual friendship, of genuine love and compassion, and foremost, this is an American story with roots that run deep in the values and traditions of the In Lion in the White House: A Life of Theodore Roosevelt, historian Aida Donald masterfully chronicles the life of this first modern president. TR’s accomplishments in office were immense. As President, Roosevelt redesigned the office of Chief Executive and the workings of the Republican Party to meet the challenges of the new industrial economy. Believing that the emerging aristocracy of wealth represented a genuine threat to democracy, TR broke trusts to curb the rapacity of big business. He improved economic and social conditions for the average American. Roosevelt built the Panama Canal and engaged the country in world affairs, putting a temporary end to American isolationism. And he won the Nobel Peace Prize-the only sitting president ever so honored. Throughout his public career, TR fought valiantly to steer the GOP back to its noblest ideals as embodied by Abraham Lincoln. Alas, his hopes for his party were quashed by the GOP’s strong rightward turn in the years after he left office. But his vision for America lives on. It was their deep and passionate love, David’s extraordinary insight into all aspects of nature, and the tragedy of his early death that inspired Daphne’s vast array of achievements, most notably the founding of the world-renowned David Sheldrick Wildlife Trust and the Orphans’ Nursery in Nairobi National Park, where Daphne continues to live and work to this day. \n \nEncompassing not only David and Daphne’s tireless campaign for an end to poaching and for conserving Kenya’s wildlife, but also their ability to engage with the human side of animals and their rearing of the orphans expressly so One thing is clear: We are witnessing the reshaping of the presidency. Jonathan Karl brings us into the White House in a powerful book unlike any other on the Trump administration. He’s known and covered Donald Trump longer than any other White House reporter.  With extraordinary access to Trump during the campaign and at 1600 Pennsylvania Avenue, Karl delivers essential new reporting and surprising insights.  These are the behind-the-scenes moments that define Trump’s presidency--an extraordinary look at the president, the person, and those closest to him. This is the real story of Trump’s unlikely rise; of the struggles and battles of those who work in the administration and those who report on it; of the plots and schemes of a senior staff enduring stunning and unprecedented unpredictability. Karl takes us from a TV set turned campaign office to the strange quiet of Trump’s White House on Inauguration Day to a high-powered reelection campaign set to change the country’s course. He shows us an administration rewriting the role of the president on the fly and a press corps that has never been more vital. Above all, this book is only possible because of the surprisingly open relationship Donald Trump has had with Jonathan Karl, a reporter he has praised, fought, and branded an enemy of the people. This is Front Row at the Trump Show.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11488480626381625697\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div For thirteen years - the worst in Zimbabwe\'s volatile history - this intrepid Australian woman lived in the Hwange bush fighting for the lives of these elephants, forming an extraordinary and life-changing bond with them.Now remote from Robert Mugabe\'s rule, Sharon writes without restraint sequentially through the years, taking us on a truly unforgettable ride of hope and heartbreak, profound love and loss, adversity and new beginnings. This is the haunting, all-encompassing story we\'ve been waiting for.Powerfully moving, sometimes disturbing and often very funny, Elephant Dawn is a celebration of love, courage and honour amongst our greatest land mammals. With resilience beyond measure, Sharon earns the supreme right to call them family.[The book includes 32 pages of colour photographs.]<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10339156723174397406\" href=\"#\"             <span class="readable">&ldquo;Those of us who are in tune with nature and animals know it is our way of life, Bram. There is a connection to all living things, a vibration of Life. Animals were not given a power of choice. A lion does not try and eat legumes, nor an elephant meat. We believe the best way to communicate with nature, God, is through a liaison: the animals..... Nature hears one voice and obeys it. That is why ten or ten thousand birds may rise from the surface of a lake at the same time and yet never touch one another. Man only hears his own voice. He constantly bumps into another. Even his voice mirrors his erratic walk, jealousy, hate, ego, pride, lying, cheating. He makes his own judgements and falls prey to his greed. Remember, the moon is reflected on one drop of water as is the entire ocean-- so it is with God. He is reflected ins each living thing-- in a grain of sand as the entire shore, one star as the whole universe. Each animal as in all creatures. -Jagrat&rdquo;</span>
